	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Communist state</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">State that aims to achieve socialism and then communism</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about sovereign states governed by Communist parties. For the social movement and political ideology, see <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">Communism</a>. For the hypothetical social stage proposed by Marxist theory, see <a href="/wiki/Communist_society" title="Communist society">Communist society</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>

<p>A <b>Communist state</b> (sometimes referred to as <b><a href="/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism" title="Marxism–Leninism">Marxist–Leninist</a> state</b> or <b>workers' state</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">state</a> that is administered and governed by a <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">single party</a>, guided by Marxist–Leninist philosophy.
</p><p>There have been several instances of Communist states with functioning <a href="/wiki/Participation_(decision_making)" title="Participation (decision making)">political participation</a> processes involving several other non-party organisations, such as <a href="/wiki/Trade_unions" class="mw-redirect" title="Trade unions">trade unions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Committee" title="Committee">factory committees</a> and <a href="/wiki/Direct_democracy" title="Direct democracy">direct democratic</a> participation.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The term "Communist state" is used by Western historians, political scientists and media to refer to these countries. However, contrary to Western usage, these states do not describe themselves as "communist" nor do they claim to have achieved communism—they refer to themselves as <a href="/wiki/Socialist_state" title="Socialist state">Socialist or Workers' states</a> that are in the process of constructing <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Economics_of_Socialism_after_World_War_Two:_1945-1990_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Economics_of_Socialism_after_World_War_Two:_1945-1990-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Williams_1983_289_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Williams_1983_289-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Communist states are typically administered by a single, <a href="/wiki/Democratic_centralism" title="Democratic centralism">centralised party apparatus</a>, although some provide the impression of multiple political parties but these are all solely in control by that centralised party. These parties usually are Marxist–Leninist or some variation thereof (including <a href="/wiki/Maoism" title="Maoism">Maoism</a> in <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>), with the official aim of achieving socialism and progressing toward a <a href="/wiki/Communist_society" title="Communist society">communist society</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_of_Communist_states">Development of Communist states</span></h2>
<p>During the 20th century, the world's first constitutionally socialist state was in Russia in 1917. In 1922, it <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Creation_of_the_USSR" title="Treaty on the Creation of the USSR">joined</a> other former territories of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">empire</a> to become the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Union of Soviet Socialist Republics</a> (USSR). After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Army" title="Soviet Army">Soviet Army</a> occupied much of Eastern Europe and thus helped establish Communist states in these countries. Most Communist states in Eastern Europe were <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">allied</a> with the Soviet Union, except for <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> which declared itself <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">non-aligned</a>. In 1949, after a <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">war against Japanese occupation</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">civil war</a> resulting in a <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" title="Communist Party of China">Communist</a> victory, the <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People's Republic of China</a> (PRC) was established. Communist states were also established in <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>. A Communist state was established in <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>, although it later adopted its own ideology called <a href="/wiki/Juche" title="Juche">Juche</a>. In 1989, the Communist states in Eastern Europe collapsed under public pressure during a <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989" title="Revolutions of 1989">wave of non-violent movements</a> which led to the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a> in 1991. Today, the existing Communist states in the world are in China, Cuba, Laos and Vietnam.
</p><p>These Communist states often do not claim to have achieved socialism or communism in their countries—rather, they claim to be building and working toward the establishment of socialism in their countries. For example, the preamble to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Vietnam" title="Constitution of Vietnam">Socialist Republic of Vietnam's Constitution</a> states that Vietnam only entered a transition stage between <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialism</a> after the country was re-unified under the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Vietnam" title="Communist Party of Vietnam">Communist Party</a> in 1976<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Cuba" title="Constitution of Cuba">1992 Constitution of the Republic of Cuba</a> states that the role of the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Cuba" title="Communist Party of Cuba">Communist Party</a> is to "guide the common effort toward the goals and construction of socialism".<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li><a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a></li></ul>
</div></td>
</tr><tr><th class="navbox-abovebelow" style="padding:0.1em;line-height:1.2em;padding:0.3em;">
<a href="/wiki/Post-Soviet_states" title="Post-Soviet states">Post-Soviet states</a></th></tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 10em; -webkit-column-width: 10em; column-width: 10em; text-align:left">

<li><a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a></li></ul>
</div></td>
</tr><tr><td class="navbox-abovebelow" style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold">
<a href="/wiki/Portal:Communism" title="Portal:Communism">Communism portal</a></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:History_of_Communist_Nations" title="Template:History of Communist Nations"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:History_of_Communist_Nations" title="Template talk:History of Communist Nations"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:History_of_Communist_Nations&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Communist states share similar institutions, which are organized on the premise that the <a href="/wiki/Communist_party" title="Communist party">Communist party</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Vanguardism" title="Vanguardism">vanguard of the proletariat</a> and represents the long-term interests of the people. The doctrine of <a href="/wiki/Democratic_centralism" title="Democratic centralism">democratic centralism</a>, which was developed by <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a> as a set of principles to be used in the internal affairs of the Communist party, is extended to society at large.<sup id="cite_ref-Furtak,_Robert_K._1986,_pp._8–9_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Furtak,_Robert_K._1986,_pp._8–9-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to democratic centralism, all leaders must be elected by the people and all proposals must be debated openly, but once a decision has been reached all people have a duty to obey that decision and all debate should end. When used within a political party, democratic centralism is meant to prevent factionalism and splits. When applied to an entire state, democratic centralism creates a <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">one-party system</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Furtak,_Robert_K._1986,_pp._8–9_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Furtak,_Robert_K._1986,_pp._8–9-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The constitutions of most Communist states describe their political system as a form of democracy.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> They thus recognize the sovereignty of the people as embodied in a series of <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative</a> parliamentary institutions. Such states do not have a <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">separation of powers</a> and instead have one national legislative body (such as the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Soviet" title="Supreme Soviet">Supreme Soviet</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>) which is considered the highest organ of state power and which is legally superior to the executive and judicial branches of government.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Such national legislative politics in Communist states often have a similar structure to the parliaments that exist in <a href="/wiki/Liberal_democracy" title="Liberal democracy">liberal republics</a>, with two significant differences: first, the deputies elected to these national legislative bodies are not expected to represent the interests of any particular constituency, but the long-term interests of the people as a whole; and second, against Marx's advice, the legislative bodies of Communist states are not in permanent session. Rather, they convene once or several times per year in sessions which usually last only a few days.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>When the national legislative body is not in session, its powers are transferred to a smaller council (often called a <a href="/wiki/Presidium" title="Presidium">presidium</a>) which combines legislative and executive power and in some Communist states (such as the Soviet Union before 1990), acts as a collective <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>. In some systems, the presidium is composed of important Communist party members who vote the resolutions of the Communist party into law.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State_social_institutions">State social institutions</span></h3>
<p>A feature of Communist states is the existence of numerous state-sponsored social organizations (<a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">trade unions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Youth_organization" class="mw-redirect" title="Youth organization">youth organizations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_organization" class="mw-redirect" title="Women&#39;s organization">women's organizations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Club_(organization)" title="Club (organization)">associations</a> of teachers, writers, journalists and other professionals, <a href="/wiki/Consumer_cooperatives" class="mw-redirect" title="Consumer cooperatives">consumer cooperatives</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sports_club" title="Sports club">sports clubs</a> and so on) which are integrated into the political system.
</p><p>In Communist states, the social organizations are expected to promote social unity and cohesion, to serve as a link between the government and society and to provide a forum for recruitment of new Communist party members.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_power">Political power</span></h3>
<p>Historically, the political organization of many socialist states has been dominated by a one-party monopoly. Some Communist governments, such as those in <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="List of political parties in the People&#39;s Republic of China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Front_(East_Germany)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Front (East Germany)">East Germany</a> or <a href="/wiki/National_Front_(Czechoslovakia)#1948–1990" title="National Front (Czechoslovakia)">Czechoslovakia</a>, have or had more than one political party, but all minor parties are or were required to follow the leadership of the Communist party. In Communist states, the government may not tolerate criticism of policies that have already been implemented in the past or are being implemented in the present.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nevertheless, Communist parties have won elections and governed in the context of <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party democracies</a> without seeking to establish a one-party state and therefore these entities do not fall under the definition of Communist state. Examples include <a href="/wiki/San_Marino" title="San Marino">San Marino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a> (1979–1990),<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a> (presently), <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> and the Indian states of <a href="/wiki/Kerala" title="Kerala">Kerala</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Bengal" title="West Bengal">West Bengal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tripura" title="Tripura">Tripura</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Criticisms_of_communist_party_rule" class="mw-redirect" title="Criticisms of communist party rule">Criticisms of communist party rule</a></div>
<p>Countries such as the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> were criticized by Western authors and organisations on the basis of a lack of <a href="/wiki/Multi-party" class="mw-redirect" title="Multi-party">multi-party</a> <a href="/wiki/Western_democracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Western democracy">Western democracy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Basic_Books_AZ_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Basic_Books_AZ-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> in addition to several other areas where socialist society and <a href="/wiki/Western_society" class="mw-redirect" title="Western society">Western societies</a> differed. For instance, socialist societies were commonly characterised by <a href="/wiki/State_ownership" title="State ownership">state ownership</a> or <a href="/wiki/Social_ownership" title="Social ownership">social ownership</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Means_of_production" title="Means of production">means of production</a> either through <a href="/wiki/Management" title="Management">administration</a> through <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist Party">party</a> organisations, democratically elected <a href="/wiki/Councils" class="mw-redirect" title="Councils">councils</a> and <a href="/wiki/Communes" class="mw-redirect" title="Communes">communes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Co-operative" class="mw-redirect" title="Co-operative">co-operative structures</a>—in opposition to the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_democracy" title="Liberal democracy">liberal democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalist</a> <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">free market</a> paradigm of management, ownership and control by corporations and private individuals.<sup id="cite_ref-University_of_Chicago_Press_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-University_of_Chicago_Press-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Communist states have also been criticised for the <a href="/wiki/Social_influence" title="Social influence">influence</a> and outreach of their respective <a href="/wiki/Ruling_party" title="Ruling party">ruling parties</a> on <a href="/wiki/Society" title="Society">society</a>, in addition to lack of recognition for some Western <a href="/wiki/Legal_rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Legal rights">legal rights</a> and <a href="/wiki/Civil_liberty" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil liberty">liberties</a> <sup id="cite_ref-coe_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coe-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> such as the right to ownership of private property and the restriction of the <a href="/wiki/Free_speech" class="mw-redirect" title="Free speech">right to free speech</a>. The early economic development policies of Communist states have been criticised for focusing primarily on the development of <a href="/wiki/Heavy_industry" title="Heavy industry">heavy industry</a>.
</p><p>Soviet advocates and socialists responded to these criticisms by highlighting the ideological differences in the concept of "freedom". McFarland and Ageyev noted that "Marxist–Leninist norms disparaged <i>laissez-faire</i> individualism (as when housing is determined by one's ability to pay), also [condemning] wide variations in personal wealth as the West has not. Instead, Soviet ideals emphasized equality—free education and medical care, little disparity in housing or salaries, and so forth".<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> When asked to comment on the claim that former citizens of Communist states enjoy increased freedoms, <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Kessler" title="Heinz Kessler">Heinz Kessler</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_National_Defence_(East_Germany)" title="Ministry of National Defence (East Germany)">East German Minister of National Defence</a>, replied: "Millions of people in Eastern Europe are now free from employment, free from safe streets, free from health care, free from social security".<sup id="cite_ref-City_Lights_Books_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-City_Lights_Books-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In his critique of states run under Marxist–Leninist ideology, economist <a href="/wiki/Michael_Ellman" title="Michael Ellman">Michael Ellman</a> of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Amsterdam" title="University of Amsterdam">University of Amsterdam</a> notes that such states compared favorably with Western states in some health indicators such as infant mortality and life expectancy.<sup id="cite_ref-ellman_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ellman-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Philipp_Ther&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Philipp Ther (page does not exist)">Philipp Ther</a><sup class="noprint" style="font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philipp_Ther" class="extiw" title="de:Philipp Ther">de</a>&#93;</sup> posits that there was an increase in the standard of living throughout <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a> countries as the result of modernization programs under Communist governments.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Similarly, <a href="/wiki/Amartya_Sen" title="Amartya Sen">Amartya Sen's</a> own analysis of international comparisons of life expectancy found that several Marxist–Leninist states made significant gains and commented "one thought that is bound to occur is that communism is good for poverty removal".<sup id="cite_ref-wilkinson_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wilkinson-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a> was followed by a rapid increase in poverty,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> crime,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> corruption,<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CPI2015_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPI2015-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> unemployment,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> homelessness,<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> rates of disease<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> and income inequality,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> along with decreases in calorie intake, life expectancy, adult literacy and income.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_Communist_states">List of Communist states</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_socialist_states" title="List of socialist states">List of socialist states</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_Communist_states">Current Communist states</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic" title="People&#39;s Republic">People's Republic</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Communist_States.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Communist_States.svg/300px-Communist_States.svg.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Communist_States.svg/450px-Communist_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Communist_States.svg/600px-Communist_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="940" data-file-height="415" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Communist_States.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of Communist states (1993–present)</div></div></div>

They are listed here together with the year of their founding and their respective ruling parties.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Multi-party_states_with_governing_Communist_parties">Multi-party states with governing Communist parties</span></h3>
<p>There are multi-party states with Communist parties leading the government. Such states are not considered to be Communist states as the countries themselves allow for multiple parties and do not provide a constitutional role for their Communist parties.
</p>
<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Flag_of_Nepal.svg/16px-Flag_of_Nepal.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Flag_of_Nepal.svg/25px-Flag_of_Nepal.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Flag_of_Nepal.svg/33px-Flag_of_Nepal.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="726" data-file-height="885" />&#160;&#160;&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Nepal_Communist_Party" title="Nepal Communist Party">Nepal Communist Party</a> is the current ruling party of the central government.</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/23px-Flag_of_India.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/35px-Flag_of_India.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/45px-Flag_of_India.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1350" data-file-height="900" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_India_(Marxist)" title="Communist Party of India (Marxist)">Communist Party of India (Marxist)</a> is the leading party in the state government in the southern state of <a href="/wiki/Kerala" title="Kerala">Kerala</a>.</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/22px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png" decoding="async" width="22" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/33px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/43px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="504" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Brazil" title="Communist Party of Brazil">Communist Party of Brazil</a> is the leading party in the state government in the northern state of <a href="/wiki/Maranh%C3%A3o" title="Maranhão">Maranhão</a>.</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Russian_Federation" title="Communist Party of the Russian Federation">Communist Party of the Russian Federation</a> is the leading party in the regional governments of the <a href="/wiki/Irkutsk_Oblast" title="Irkutsk Oblast">Irkutsk Oblast</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Oryol_Oblast" title="Oryol Oblast">Oryol Oblast</a>.</li></ul>
<p><a href="/wiki/San_Marino" title="San Marino">San Marino</a> (1945–1957), <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a> (2001–2009), <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> (2001–2013) and <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a> (1992–2015) have also had officially Communist ruling parties.
</p>

<p><b>Notes</b>
</p>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-47"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-47">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Socialist state although the government's official ideology is now the <i><a href="/wiki/Juche" title="Juche">Juche</a></i> part of <a href="/wiki/Kimilsungism%E2%80%93Kimjongilism" class="mw-redirect" title="Kimilsungism–Kimjongilism">Kimilsungism–Kimjongilism</a> policy of <a href="/wiki/Kim_Il-sung" title="Kim Il-sung">Kim Il-sung</a>, as opposed to traditional <a href="/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism" title="Marxism–Leninism">Marxism–Leninism</a>. In 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_North_Korea" title="Constitution of North Korea">Constitution of North Korea</a> was quietly amended so that not only did it remove all Marxist–Leninist references present in the first draft, but it also dropped all reference to "Communism".<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

<li id="cite_note-The_Economics_of_Socialism_after_World_War_Two:_1945-1990-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-The_Economics_of_Socialism_after_World_War_Two:_1945-1990_6-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Wilczynski, J. Aldine Transaction. p.&#160;21. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0202362281" title="Special:BookSources/978-0202362281"><bdi>978-0202362281</bdi></a>. <q>Contrary to Western usage, these countries describe themselves as 'Socialist' (not 'Communist'). The second stage (Marx's 'higher phase'), or 'Communism' is to be marked by an age of plenty, distribution according to needs (not work), the absence of money and the market mechanism, the disappearance of the last vestiges of capitalism and the ultimate 'whithering away' of the State.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Economics+of+Socialism+after+World+War+Two%3A+1945-1990&amp;rft.pages=21&amp;rft.pub=Aldine+Transaction&amp;rft.date=2008&amp;rft.isbn=978-0202362281&amp;rft.aulast=Wilczynski&amp;rft.aufirst=J.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACommunist+state" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Steele, David Ramsay (September 1999). <i>From Marx to Mises: Post Capitalist Society and the Challenge of Economic Calculation</i>. Open Court. p.&#160;45. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0875484495" title="Special:BookSources/978-0875484495"><bdi>978-0875484495</bdi></a>. <q>Among Western journalists the term 'Communist' came to refer exclusively to regimes and movements associated with the Communist International and its offspring: regimes which insisted that they were not communist but socialist, and movements which were barely communist in any sense at all.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=From+Marx+to+Mises%3A+Post+Capitalist+Society+and+the+Challenge+of+Economic+Calculation&amp;rft.pages=45&amp;rft.pub=Open+Court&amp;rft.date=1999-09&amp;rft.isbn=978-0875484495&amp;rft.aulast=Steele&amp;rft.aufirst=David+Ramsay&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACommunist+state" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-8">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Rosser, Mariana V. and J Barkley Jr. (23 July 2003). <i>Comparative Economics in a Transforming World Economy</i>. MIT Press. p.&#160;14. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0262182348" title="Special:BookSources/978-0262182348"><bdi>978-0262182348</bdi></a>. <q>Ironically, the ideological father of communism, Karl Marx, claimed that communism entailed the withering away of the state. The dictatorship of the proletariat was to be a strictly temporary phenomenon. Well aware of this, the Soviet Communists never claimed to have achieved communism, always labeling their own system socialist rather than communist and viewing their system as in transition to communism.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Comparative+Economics+in+a+Transforming+World+Economy&amp;rft.pages=14&amp;rft.pub=MIT+Press&amp;rft.date=2003-07-23&amp;rft.isbn=978-0262182348&amp;rft.aulast=Rosser&amp;rft.aufirst=Mariana+V.+and+J+Barkley+Jr.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACommunist+state" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Williams_1983_289-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Williams_1983_289_9-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Williams, Raymond (1983). "Socialism". <span class="cs1-lock-registration" title="Free registration required"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/keywordsvocabula00willrich"><i>Keywords: A vocabulary of culture and society, revised edition</i></a></span>. Oxford University Press. p.&#160;289. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-19-520469-8" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-19-520469-8"><bdi>978-0-19-520469-8</bdi></a>. <q>The decisive distinction between socialist and communist, as in one sense these terms are now ordinarily used, came with the renaming, in 1918, of the Russian Social-Democratic Labour Party (Bolsheviks) as the All-Russian Communist Party (Bolsheviks). From that time on, a distinction of socialist from communist, often with supporting definitions such as social democrat or democratic socialist, became widely current, although it is significant that all communist parties, in line with earlier usage, continued to describe themselves as socialist and dedicated to socialism.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Socialism&amp;rft.btitle=Keywords%3A+A+vocabulary+of+culture+and+society%2C+revised+edition&amp;rft.pages=289&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft.date=1983&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-19-520469-8&amp;rft.aulast=Williams&amp;rft.aufirst=Raymond&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Farchive.org%2Fdetails%2Fkeywordsvocabula00willrich&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACommunist+state" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.vietnamembassy-usa.org/learn_about_vietnam/politics/constitution/">"VN Embassy - Constitution of 1992"</a>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20110709162321/http://www.vietnamembassy-usa.org/learn_about_vietnam/politics/constitution/">Archived</a> 9 July 2011 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a> Full Text. From the Preamble: "On 2 July 1976, the National Assembly of reunified Vietnam decided to change the country's name to the Socialist Republic of Vietnam; the country entered a period of transition to socialism, strove for national construction, and unyieldingly defended its frontiers while fulfilling its internationalist duty".</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.cubanet.org/ref/dis/const_92_e.htm">"Cubanet - Constitution of the Republic of Cuba, 1992"</a>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20110709122434/http://www.cubanet.org/ref/dis/const_92_e.htm">Archived</a> 9 July 2011 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a> Full Text. From Article 5: "The Communist Party of Cuba, a follower of Martí's ideas and of Marxism-Leninism, and the organized vanguard of the Cuban nation, is the highest leading force of society and of the state, which organizes and guides the common effort toward the goals of the construction of socialism and the progress toward a communist society".</span>
